class="agent">Ajuntament de Val√®ncia</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;‚Ä¢&#160;<a href="/wiki/Alcalde" title="Alcalde">Mayor</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Joan_Rib%C3%B3_i_Canut" class="mw-redirect" title="Joan Rib√≥ i Canut">Joan Rib√≥ i Canut</a> (2019) (<a href="/wiki/Comprom%C3%ADs" class="mw-redirect" title="Comprom√≠s">Comprom√≠s</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left">Area<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th (51.99&#160;sq&#160;mi)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;‚Ä¢&#160;Urban<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th><td>628.81&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (242.78&#160;sq&#160;mi)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Elevation<div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th><td>15&#160;m (49&#160;ft)</td></tr><tr id="cite_ref-WorldUrbanAreas_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldUrbanAreas-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;‚Ä¢&#160;<a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">Metro</a><div style="font-weight:normal;display:inline;"></div></th><td>2,522,383<sup id="cite_ref-MetroRegion_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetroRegion-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Demonym" title="Demonym">Demonym(s)</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/Valencian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian people">Valencian</a> <br /> <i>valenci√†</i>,&#160;<i>-ana</i>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">va</a>)<br /><i>valenciano</i>,&#160;<i>-na</i>&#160;(<a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">es</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time style="white-space:nowrap">&#160;‚Ä¢&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</span></th><td><a href="/wiki/UTC%2B02:00" title="UTC+02:00">UTC+02:00</a> (CEST (GMT))</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Postcode</th><td class="adr"><div class="postal-code">46000-46080</div></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:ES" title="ISO 3166-2:ES">ISO 3166-2</a></th><td>ES-V</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.valencia.es">www.valencia.es</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Valencia</b> (<small>Spanish:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[baÀàlenŒ∏ja]</a></span>), officially <b>Val√®ncia</b> (<small>Valencian:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[vaÀàlensia]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Spain" title="Municipalities of Spain">third-largest city</a> in Spain after <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, with around 800,000 inhabitants in the administrative centre. Its urban area extends beyond the administrative city limits with a population of around 1.6&#160;million people.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldUrbanAreas_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldUrbanAreas-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MdFdE_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MdFdE-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Valencia is Spain's <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Spain" title="List of metropolitan areas in Spain">third largest metropolitan area</a>, with a population ranging from 1.7 to 2.5&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-MetroRegion_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetroRegion-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> depending on how the metropolitan area is defined.  The <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Valencia" title="Port of Valencia">Port of Valencia</a> is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_ports_in_Europe" title="List of busiest ports in Europe">5th busiest container port in Europe</a> and the busiest container port on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>.  The city is ranked at Beta-<a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Globalization_and_World_Cities_Research_Network" title="Globalization and World Cities Research Network">Globalization and World Cities Research Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GAWC_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAWC-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Valencia was founded as a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman</a> colony by the consul <a href="/wiki/Decimus_Junius_Brutus_Callaicus" title="Decimus Junius Brutus Callaicus">Decimus Junius Brutus Callaicus</a> in 138 BC, and called <i>Valentia Edetanorum</i>. In 714 Moroccan and Arab <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> occupied the city, introducing their language, religion and customs; they implemented improved irrigation systems and the cultivation of new crops as well.  Valencia was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Valencia" title="Taifa of Valencia">Taifa of Valencia</a>. In 1238 the Christian king <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a> conquered the city and divided the land among the nobles who helped him conquer it, as witnessed in the <i><a href="/wiki/Llibre_del_Repartiment_(Valencia)" title="Llibre del Repartiment (Valencia)">Llibre del Repartiment</a></i>. He also created a new law for the city, the <a href="/wiki/Furs_of_Valencia" title="Furs of Valencia">Furs of Valencia</a>, which were extended to the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Kingdom of Valencia</a>. In the 18th century <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V of Spain</a> abolished the privileges as punishment to the kingdom of Valencia for aligning with the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Habsburg side</a> in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>. Valencia was the capital of Spain when <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a> moved the Court there in the summer of 1812. It also served as capital between 1936 and 1937, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Second Spanish Republic</a>.
</p><p>The city is situated on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Turia_(river)" title="Turia (river)">Turia</a>, on the east coast of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, fronting the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Valencia" title="Gulf of Valencia">Gulf of Valencia</a> on the Mediterranean Sea. Its historic centre is one of the largest in Spain, with approximately 169&#160;ha (420 acres);<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> this heritage of ancient monuments, views and cultural attractions makes Valencia one of the country's most popular tourist destinations.
</p><p>Due to its long history, this is a city with numerous popular celebrations and traditions, such as the <i><a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Fallas</a></i> (featuring the traditional Spanish dish <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a></i>), which were declared as <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_of_National_Tourist_Interest_of_Spain" title="Fiestas of National Tourist Interest of Spain">Fiestas of National Tourist Interest of Spain</a> in 1965<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">Intangible cultural heritage</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in November 2016. From 1991 to 2015, <a href="/wiki/Rita_Barber%C3%A1_Nolla" class="mw-redirect" title="Rita Barber√° Nolla">Rita Barber√° Nolla</a> was the mayor of the city, yet in 2015, <a href="/wiki/Joan_Rib%C3%B3_i_Canut" class="mw-redirect" title="Joan Rib√≥ i Canut">Joan Rib√≥</a> from <a href="/wiki/Coalici%C3%B3_Comprom%C3%ADs" title="Coalici√≥ Comprom√≠s">Coalici√≥ Comprom√≠s</a>, became mayor.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg/140px-Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg/210px-Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg/280px-Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sello_plaza_de_la_virgen_valencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Roman Cornucopia, symbol of Valentia, found on the floor of a Roman building excavated in the Pla√ßa de la Mare de D√©u.</div></div></div><p>
The original <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> name of the city was Valentia (<small>IPA:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Latin" title="Help:IPA/Latin">[waÀàl…õnt…™a]</a></span>), meaning "strength", or "valour", the city being named according to the Roman practice of recognising the valour of former Roman soldiers after a war. The Roman historian <a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">Livy</a> explains that the founding of Valentia in the 2nd century BC was due to the settling of the Roman soldiers who fought against an Iberian rebel, <a href="/wiki/Viriatus" class="mw-redirect" title="Viriatus">Viriatus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Astin1989_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Astin1989-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_IMG_0975-a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A_IMG_0975-a.jpg/280px-A_IMG_0975-a.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A_IMG_0975-a.jpg/420px-A_IMG_0975-a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/A_IMG_0975-a.jpg/560px-A_IMG_0975-a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="990" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_IMG_0975-a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pla√ßa de la Mare de D√©u (also called Plaza de la Virgen), iconic square of the city.</div></div></div>
<p>During the rule of the <a href="/wiki/Al_Andalus" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Andalus">Muslim kingdoms in Spain</a>, it had the nickname <i>Medina at-Tarab</i> ('City of Joy') according to one transliteration, or <i>Medina at-Turab</i> ('City of Sands') according to another, since it was located on the banks of the River Turia. It is not clear if the term <i>Balansiyya</i> was reserved for the entire <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Valencia" title="Taifa of Valencia">Taifa of Valencia</a> or also designated the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Galbis2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Galbis2009-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By gradual sound changes, <i>Valentia</i> has become <i>Valencia</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[baÀàlenŒ∏ja]</a></span> (i.e. before a <a href="/wiki/Pausa" title="Pausa">pausa</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nasal_consonant" title="Nasal consonant">nasal sound</a>) or <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[-Œ≤aÀàlenŒ∏ja]</a></span> (after a <a href="/wiki/Continuant" title="Continuant">continuant</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Castilian</a> and <i>Val√®ncia</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[vaÀàlensia]</a></span> in <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">Valencian</a>. In Valencian, <i>e</i> with grave accent (<i>√®</i>) indicates /<a href="/wiki/%C6%90_(IPA)" class="mw-redirect" title="∆ê (IPA)">…õ</a>/ in contrast to /<a href="/wiki/E_(IPA)" class="mw-redirect" title="E (IPA)">e</a>/, but the word <i>Val√®ncia</i> is an exception to this rule, since <i>√®</i> is pronounced /e/. The spelling "Val√®ncia" was approved by the <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acad√®mia Valenciana de la Llengua">AVL</a> based on tradition after a debate on the matter.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location">Location</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Location">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia,_Spain_ESA396538.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg/240px-Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg" decoding="async" width="240" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg/360px-Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg/480px-Valencia%2C_Spain_ESA396538.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2501" data-file-height="2500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia,_Spain_ESA396538.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Valencia and surroundings as seen by the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">ESA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sentinel-2" title="Sentinel-2">Sentinel-2</a> satellite.</div></div></div>
<p>Valencia stands on the banks of the <a href="/wiki/Turia_(river)" title="Turia (river)">Turia River</a>, located on the eastern coast of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> and the western part of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, fronting the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Valencia" title="Gulf of Valencia">Gulf of Valencia</a>. At its founding by the Romans, it stood on a river island in the Turia, 6.4 kilometres (4.0&#160;mi) from the sea. The <a href="/wiki/Albufera" title="Albufera">Albufera</a>, a freshwater lagoon and estuary about 11&#160;km (7&#160;mi) south of the city, is one of the largest lakes in Spain. The City Council bought the lake from the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown of Spain">Crown of Spain</a> for 1,072,980 pesetas in 1911,<sup id="cite_ref-Gonz√°lbez1960_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gonz√°lbez1960-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and today it forms the main portion of the <i>Parc Natural de l'Albufera</i> (<a href="/wiki/Albufera" title="Albufera">Albufera Nature Reserve</a>), with a surface area of 21,120 hectares (52,200 acres). In 1976, because of its cultural, historical, and ecological value, the <i>Generalitat Valenciana</i> declared it a natural park.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Valencia" title="Climate of Valencia">Climate of Valencia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg/250px-Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg/375px-Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg/500px-Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciutat_vella_vista.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Valencia has mild winters, little rain and long summers</div></div></div>
<p>Valencia has a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical climate">subtropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K√∂ppen climate classification">K√∂ppen</a> <i>Csa</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> with short, very mild winters and long, hot and dry summers.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-KGcc_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KGcc-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Its average annual temperature is 18.4&#160;¬∞C (65.1&#160;¬∞F); 23.0&#160;¬∞C (73.4&#160;¬∞F) during the day and 13.8&#160;¬∞C (56.8&#160;¬∞F) at night. 
In the coldest month, January, the maximum temperature typically during the day ranges from 14 to 21&#160;¬∞C (57 to 70&#160;¬∞F), the minimum temperature typically at night ranges from 5 to 10&#160;¬∞C (41 to 50&#160;¬∞F). In the warmest month ‚Äì August, the maximum temperature during the day typically ranges from 28 to 34&#160;¬∞C (82 to 93&#160;¬∞F), about 21 to 23&#160;¬∞C (70 to 73&#160;¬∞F) at night. Generally, similar temperatures to those experienced in the northern part of Europe in summer last about 8 months, from April to November. March is transitional, the temperature often exceeds 20&#160;¬∞C (68&#160;¬∞F), with an average temperature of 19.3&#160;¬∞C (66.7&#160;¬∞F) during the day and 10.0&#160;¬∞C (50.0&#160;¬∞F) at night. December, January and February are the coldest months, with average temperatures around 17&#160;¬∞C (63&#160;¬∞F) during the day and 8&#160;¬∞C (46&#160;¬∞F) at night. Valencia has one of the mildest winters in Europe, owing to its southern location on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Foehn" class="mw-redirect" title="Foehn">Foehn</a> phenomenon. The January average is comparable to temperatures expected for May and September in the major cities of northern Europe.
</p><p>Sunshine duration hours are 2,696 per year, from 155 (average nearly 5 hours of sunshine duration a day) in December to 315 (average above 10 hours of sunshine duration a day) in July. The average temperature of the sea is 15‚Äì16&#160;¬∞C (59‚Äì61&#160;¬∞F) during winters<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-weather2travel_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and 26‚Äì28&#160;¬∞C (79‚Äì82&#160;¬∞F) during summers.<sup id="cite_ref-weather2travel_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Average annual <a href="/wiki/Relative_humidity" title="Relative humidity">relative humidity</a> is 65%.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Banco_de_Valencia,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_135.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG/220px-Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG/330px-Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG/440px-Banco_de_Valencia%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_135.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2929" data-file-height="2691" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Banco_de_Valencia,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_135.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Banco_de_Valencia" title="Banco de Valencia">Bank of Valencia</a></div></div></div>
<p>Valencia  enjoyed strong economic growth before the economic crisis of 2008, much of it spurred by tourism and the <a href="/wiki/Construction" title="Construction">construction industry</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> with concurrent development and expansion of telecommunications and transport. The city's economy is service-oriented, as nearly 84% of the working population is employed in service sector occupations<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. However, the city still maintains an important industrial base, with 8.5% of the population employed in this sector. Growth has recently improved in the manufacturing sector, mainly automobile assembly; (The <a href="/wiki/Ford_Valencia_Plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Ford Valencia Plant">large factory</a> of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Motor_Company" title="Ford Motor Company">Ford Motor Company</a> lies in a suburb of the city, <a href="/wiki/Almussafes" title="Almussafes">Almussafes</a><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>). Agricultural activities are still carried on in the municipality, even though of relatively minor importance with only 1.9% of the working population and 3,973&#160;ha (9,820 acres) planted mostly in orchards and citrus groves.
</p><p>Since the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> (2008), Valencia had experienced a growing unemployment rate, increased government debt, etc. Severe spending cuts had been introduced by the city government.
</p><p>In 2009, Valencia was designated "the 29th fastest-improving European city".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Its influence in commerce, education, entertainment, media, fashion, science and the arts contributes to its status as one of the world's "Beta"-rank <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">global cities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GAWC_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GAWC-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Valencia metropolitan area had a <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">GDP amounting to $52.7&#160;billion</a>, and $28,141 per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-Brookings_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brookings-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Valencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/220px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/330px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Port_of_Valencia.jpg/440px-Port_of_Valencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="768" data-file-height="512" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Port_of_Valencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Valencia" title="Port of Valencia">Port of Valencia</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Port_of_Valencia" title="Port of Valencia">Valencia's port</a> is the biggest on the Mediterranean western coast,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> the first of Spain in container traffic as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> and the second of Spain<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> in total traffic, handling 20% of Spain's exports.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The main exports are foodstuffs and beverages. Other exports include oranges, furniture, ceramic tiles, fans, textiles and iron products. Valencia's <a href="/wiki/Secondary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Secondary sector of the economy">manufacturing sector</a> focuses on metallurgy, chemicals, textiles, shipbuilding and brewing. Small and medium-sized industries are an important part of the local economy, and before the current crisis unemployment was lower than the Spanish average.
</p><p>Valencia's port underwent radical changes to accommodate the 32nd <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America&#39;s Cup">America's Cup</a> in 2007. It was divided into two parts‚Äîone was unchanged while the other section was modified for the America's Cup festivities. The two sections remain divided by a wall that projects far into the water to maintain clean water for the America's Cup side.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_122.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG/330px-Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG" decoding="async" width="330" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG/495px-Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG/660px-Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_122.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4758" data-file-height="2253" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Estaci%C3%B3n_del_Norte,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_122.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Estaci%C3%B3_del_Nord_(Valencia)" title="Estaci√≥ del Nord (Valencia)">Estaci√≥ del Nord</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Public transport is provided by the <i><a href="/wiki/Ferrocarrils_de_la_Generalitat_Valenciana" title="Ferrocarrils de la Generalitat Valenciana">Ferrocarrils de la Generalitat Valenciana</a></i> (FGV), which operates the <a href="/wiki/Metrovalencia" title="Metrovalencia">Metrovalencia</a> and other rail and bus services. The <i><a href="/wiki/Estaci%C3%B3_del_Nord_(Valencia)" title="Estaci√≥ del Nord (Valencia)">Estaci√≥ del Nord</a></i> (North Station) is the main railway terminus in Valencia. A new temporary station, <i><a href="/wiki/Valencia-Joaqu%C3%ADn_Sorolla_railway_station" title="Valencia-Joaqu√≠n Sorolla railway station">Estaci√≥ de Val√®ncia-Joaqu√≠n Sorolla</a></i>, has been built on land adjacent to this terminus to accommodate high speed <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> trains to and from Madrid, Barcelona, Seville and Alicante. <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Airport" title="Valencia Airport">Valencia Airport</a> is situated 9&#160;km (5.6&#160;mi) west of Valencia city centre. <a href="/wiki/Alicante_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Alicante Airport">Alicante Airport</a> is situated about 133&#160;km (83&#160;mi) south of center of Valencia.
</p><p>The City of Valencia also makes available a <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle sharing system">bicycle sharing system</a> named <a href="/wiki/Valenbisi" title="Valenbisi">Valenbisi</a> to both visitors and residents. As of 13 October 2012, the system has 2750 bikes distributed over 250 stations all throughout the city.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Valencia_Public_Transportation_Statistics">Valencia Public Transportation Statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Valencia Public Transportation Statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The average amount of time people spend commuting with public transit in Valencia, for example to and from work, on a weekday is 44 min. 6% of public transit riders, ride for more than 2 hours every day. The average amount of time people wait at a stop or station for public transit is 10 min, while 9% of riders wait for over 20 minutes on average every day. The average distance people usually ride in a single trip with public transit is 5.9&#160;km, while 8% travel for over 12&#160;km in a single direction.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_(Valencia)_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg/220px-Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg/330px-Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg/440px-Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_%28Valencia%29_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Playa_de_la_Malvarrosa_(Valencia)_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Malvarrosa Beach</div></div></div>
<p>Starting in the mid-1990s, Valencia, formerly an industrial centre, saw rapid development that expanded its cultural and tourism possibilities, and transformed it into a newly vibrant city. Many local landmarks were restored, including the ancient Towers of the medieval city (<i>Serrans</i> Towers and <i>Quart</i> Towers), and the Saint Miquel dels Reis monastery (<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monasterio_de_San_Miguel_de_los_Reyes" class="extiw" title="es:Monasterio de San Miguel de los Reyes">es:Monasterio de San Miguel de los Reyes</a>), which now holds a conservation library. Whole sections of the old city, for example the Carmen Quarter, have been extensively renovated. The <i>Passeig Mar√≠tim</i>, a 4&#160;km (2&#160;mi)&#160;long palm tree-lined promenade was constructed along the beaches of the north side of the port <i>(Platja de Les Arenes, Platja del Cabanyal and Platja de la Malva-rosa</i>).
</p><p>The city has numerous <a href="/wiki/Convention_center" title="Convention center">convention centres</a> and venues for trade events, among them the Feria Valencia Convention and Exhibition Centre <i>(Instituci√≥n Ferial de Valencia)</i> and the <i>Palau de congres</i> (Conference Palace), and several 5-star hotels to accommodate business travelers.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg/220px-Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg/330px-Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg/440px-Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fallas2017_Masclet%C3%A0_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Locals and tourists watching the traditional "<a href="/wiki/Masclet%C3%A0" title="Masclet√†">masclet√†</a>" during <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a></div></div></div>
<p>In its long history, Valencia has acquired many local traditions and festivals, among them the <i><a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a></i>, which were declared Celebrations of International Tourist Interest <i>(Festes de Inter√©s Tur√≠stic Internacional)</i> on 25 January 1965 and UNESCO's intangible cultural heritage of humanity list on 30 November 2016, and the Water Tribunal of Valencia <i>(Tribunal de les Aig√ºes de Val√®ncia)</i>, which was declared an intangible cultural heritage of humanity <i>(Patrimoni Cultural Inmaterial de la Humanitat</i>) in 2009. In addition to these Valencia has hosted world-class events that helped shape the city's reputation and put it in the international spotlight, e.g., the Regional Exhibition of 1909, the 32nd and the 33rd <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America&#39;s Cup">America's Cup</a> competitions, the <a href="/wiki/European_Grand_Prix" title="European Grand Prix">European Grand Prix</a> of <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> auto racing, the Valencia Open 500 tennis tournament, and the Global Champions Tour of equestrian sports. The final round of the MotoGP Championship is held annually at the Circuito de la Communitat Valenciana.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/2007_America%27s_Cup" title="2007 America&#39;s Cup">2007 America's Cup</a> yachting races were held at Valencia in June and July 2007 and attracted huge crowds. The Louis Vuitton stage drew 1,044,373 visitors and the America's Cup match drew 466,010 visitors to the event.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The third largest city in Spain and the <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_of_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities of the European Union by population within city limits">24th most populous municipality</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, Valencia has a population of 809,267<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> within its administrative limits on a land area of 134.6&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (52&#160;sq&#160;mi). The <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban area</a> of Valencia extending beyond the administrative city limits has a population of between 1,564,145<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> and 1,595,000.<sup id="cite_ref-WorldUrbanAreas_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WorldUrbanAreas-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Also according to Spanish <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Development_(Spain)" title="Ministry of Development (Spain)">Ministry of Development</a>, <i>Greater Urban Area</i> (es. <i>Gran √Årea Urbana</i>) within <a href="/wiki/Horta_of_Valencia" title="Horta of Valencia">Horta of Valencia</a> has a population of 1,551,585 on area of 628,81 km¬≤, in period of 2001-2011 there was a population increase of 191,842 people, an increase of 14.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-MdFdE_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MdFdE-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> About 2 million people live in the Valencia <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>. According to the <i>CityPopulation.de</i>, metropolitan area has a population of 1,770,742<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>, according to the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organization for Economic Cooperation and Development</a>: 2,300,000<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>, according to the <a href="/wiki/World_Gazetteer" class="mw-redirect" title="World Gazetteer">World Gazetteer</a>: 2,513,965<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and according to the <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>: 2,522,383.<sup id="cite_ref-MetroRegion_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MetroRegion-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Between 2007 and 2008 there was a 14% increase in the foreign born population with the largest numeric increases by country being from Bolivia, Romania and Italy. This growth in the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_born" title="Foreign born">foreign born</a> population, which rose from 1.5% in the year 2000<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> to 9.1% in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> has also occurred in the two larger cities of Madrid and Barcelona.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The main countries of origin were Romania, United Kingdom and Bulgaria.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 10 largest groups of foreign born people by 2018 are&#160;: 
</p>
