<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paella_hirviendo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Paella_hirviendo.jpg/200px-Paella_hirviendo.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Paella_hirviendo.jpg/300px-Paella_hirviendo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Paella_hirviendo.jpg/400px-Paella_hirviendo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1331" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Paella_hirviendo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Traditional preparation of paella</div></div></div>
<p>Valencia is known internationally for the <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a> <i>(Les Falles)</i>, a local festival held in March, as well as for <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a> valenciana</i>, traditional Valencian ceramics, craftsmanship in traditional dress, and the architecture of the <a href="/wiki/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies">City of Arts and Sciences</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a> and <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Candela" title="F√©lix Candela">F√©lix Candela</a>.
</p><p>La <a href="/wiki/Tomatina" class="mw-redirect" title="Tomatina">Tomatina</a>, an annual tomato fight, draws crowds to the nearby town of Bu√±ol in August. There are also a number of well-preserved traditional Catholic festivities throughout the year. <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Holy Week</a> celebrations in Valencia are considered some of the most colourful in Spain. <sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Valencia was once the site of the <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a> <a href="/wiki/European_Grand_Prix" title="European Grand Prix">European Grand Prix</a>, first hosting the event on 24 August 2008, but was dropped at the beginning of the Grand Prix 2013 season, though still holds the annual Moto GP race at the <a href="/wiki/Circuit_Ricardo_Tormo" title="Circuit Ricardo Tormo">Circuit Ricardo Tormo</a>, usually that last race of the season in November.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Valencia" title="University of Valencia">University of Valencia</a> (officially <i>Universitat de Val√®ncia Estudi General</i>) was founded in 1499, being one of the oldest surviving universities in Spain and the oldest university in the Valencian Community. It was listed as one of the four leading Spanish universities in the 2011 Shanghai Academic Ranking of World Universities.
</p><p>In 2012, Boston's <a href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music" title="Berklee College of Music">Berklee College of Music</a> opened a satellite campus at the <a href="/wiki/Palau_de_les_Arts_Reina_Sofia" title="Palau de les Arts Reina Sofia">Palau de les Arts Reina Sofia</a>, its first and only international campus outside the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Since 2003, Valencia also hosts the music courses of Musikeon, the leading musical institution in the Spanish-speaking world.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Valencia is a <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a> city: <a href="/wiki/Valencian_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> are the two <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>. Spanish is official in all of Spain, whereas Valencian is official in the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian Community</a>. Despite distinct <a href="/wiki/Catalan_dialects" title="Catalan dialects">dialectal traits</a> and <a href="/wiki/Valencian_language_controversy" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencian language controversy">political tension</a> between Catalonia and Valencia, Catalan and Valencian are mutually intelligible and considered two varieties of the same language by the linguistic academies and governments of both regions, just under different names.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Valencian has been historically de-emphasised in favour of Spanish. The effects have been more noticeable in the city proper where its daily use is favoured by only 10% of the population, although virtually all know Valencian to one degree or another. This situation also applies in the city of Alicante, population 350,000, the southernmost section of Alicante province with 400,000 inhabitants, and the traditionally Spanish-speaking population in the western regions of the Valencian Community. Whereas the language has remained active in the rural, coastal and metropolitan areas which have a population of 3.4 million. Ability to understand Valencian approaches 80% overall and fluency is 57% in a population of 5 million. If the Spanish-speaking regions with 500,000 are not included comprehension is about 85% and fluency rises to 62%.
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castille" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabella I of Castille">Castille-Aragon unification</a>, a Spanish-speaking elite established itself in the city.The upper classes in Valenician favoured Spanish while the opposite was the case in Catalonia.  In more recent history, the establishment of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Franco</a>'s military and administrative apparatus in Valencia further excluded Valencian from public life. Valencian recovered its official status, prestige and use in education after the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">transition to democracy</a> in 1978. However, due to industrialisation in recent decades, Valencia has attracted immigration from other regions in Spain, and hence there is also a demographic factor for its declining social use. Due to a combination of these reasons, Valencia has become the bastion of anti-Catalan <a href="/wiki/Blaverism" title="Blaverism">blaverism</a>, which celebrates Valencian as merely folkloric, but rejects the existing standard which was adapted from Catalan orthography.
</p><p>Spanish is currently the predominant language in the city proper.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the education system, most Valencians know Spanish and Valencian, and either can be used in the city. Valencia is therefore the second biggest Catalan-speaking city after <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. Institutional buildings and streets are named in Valencian. The city is also home to many pro-Valencian political and civil organisations. Furthermore, education entirely in Valencian is offered in more than 70 state-owned schools in the city, as well as by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Valencia" title="University of Valencia">University of Valencia</a> across all disciplines.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Valencian_cuisine" title="Valencian cuisine">Valencian cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg/200px-Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg/300px-Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg/400px-Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Horchata_de_chufa_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glass of <a href="/wiki/Orxata" class="mw-redirect" title="Orxata">orxata de xufa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fartons" title="Fartons">fartons</a> sweets.</div></div></div>
<p>Valencia is known for its gastronomic culture. The <i><a href="/wiki/Paella" title="Paella">paella</a></i> (a simmered rice dish with meat (usually chicken or rabbit) or seafood) was born in Valencia; Other traditional dishes of Valencian gastronomy includes "<a href="/wiki/Fideu%C3%A0" title="Fideu√†">fideu√†</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Arr%C3%B2s_a_banda" title="Arr√≤s a banda">arr√≤s a banda</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Arr%C3%B2s_negre" title="Arr√≤s negre">arr√≤s negre</a>" (black rice), "<a href="/wiki/Fartons" title="Fartons">fartons</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Bu%C3%B1uelos" class="mw-redirect" title="Bu√±uelos">bunyols</a>", the <a href="/wiki/Tortilla_de_patatas" class="mw-redirect" title="Tortilla de patatas">Spanish omelette</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Pincho" title="Pincho">pinchos</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Tapas" title="Tapas">tapas</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Squid_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Squid (food)">calamares</a>"(squid).
</p><p>Valencia was also the birthplace of the cold <i><a href="/wiki/Cyperus_esculentus" title="Cyperus esculentus">xufa</a></i> beverage known as <i><a href="/wiki/Orxata" class="mw-redirect" title="Orxata">orxata</a></i>, popular in many parts of the world, including the Americas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Natura_Mare_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg/170px-Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg/255px-Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg/340px-Natura_Mare_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="783" data-file-height="1178" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Natura_Mare_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Falla Na Jordana 2003 (winner)</div></div></div>
<dl><dt>Falles of Valencia</dt></dl>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a></div>
<p>Every year, the five days and nights from 15 to 19 March, called <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a>, are a continual festival in Valencia; beginning on 1 March, the popular pyrotechnic events called <i><a href="/wiki/Masclet%C3%A0" title="Masclet√†">masclet√†es</a></i> start every day at 2:00 pm. The <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Falles</a> (<i>Fallas</i> in Spanish) is an enduring tradition in Valencia and other towns in the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian Community</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fiestas_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiestas-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> where it has become an important tourist attraction. The festival began in the 18th century,<sup id="cite_ref-fallasvalencia.es_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fallasvalencia.es-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and came to be celebrated on the night of the feast day of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a>, the patron saint of carpenters, with the burning of waste planks of wood from their workshops, as well as worn-out wooden objects brought by people in the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-RodgersRodgers2002_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RodgersRodgers2002-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This tradition continued to evolve, and eventually the <i>parots</i> were dressed with clothing to look like people‚Äîthese were the first <i>ninots</i>, with features identifiable as being those of a well-known person from the neighborhood often added as well. In 1901 the city inaugurated the awarding of prizes for the best Falles monuments,<sup id="cite_ref-fallasvalencia.es_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fallasvalencia.es-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and neighborhood groups still vie with each other to make the most impressive and outrageous creations.<sup id="cite_ref-Villarroya1992_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Villarroya1992-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Their intricate assemblages, placed on top of pedestals for better visibility, depict famous personalities and topical subjects of the past year, presenting humorous and often satirical commentary on them.
</p><p>19 March at night Valencians burn all the Falles in an event called "La Crem√†".
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Valencia" title="History of Valencia">History of Valencia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Valencia" title="Timeline of Valencia">Timeline of Valencia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_colony">Roman colony</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Roman colony">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg/140px-Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg/210px-Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg/280px-Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3864" data-file-height="5152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Arqueol%C3%B3gico_de_la_Almoina_21.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Archaeological Center of la Almoina contains a large collection of remains of the Roman city of <i>Valentia Edetanorum</i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Valencia is one of the oldest cities in Spain, founded in the Roman period, c. 138 BC, under the name "Valentia Edetanorum". A few centuries later, with the power vacuum left by the demise of the Roman imperial administration, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> assumed the reins of power in the city, coinciding with the first waves of the invading Germanic peoples (<a href="/wiki/Suevi" class="mw-redirect" title="Suevi">Suevi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alans" title="Alans">Alans</a>, and later the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Muslim_rule">Muslim rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Muslim rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel,_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG/170px-Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG/255px-Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG/340px-Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel%2C_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2748" data-file-height="3664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_de_l%27%C3%80ngel,_Val%C3%A8ncia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "Tower del √Ångel" formed part of the Muslim Walls of Valencia</div></div></div>
<p>The city surrendered to the invading Moors (Berbers and Arabs) about 714 AD,<sup id="cite_ref-Sanz2003_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanz2003-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and the cathedral of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_of_Saragossa" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Vincent of Saragossa">Saint Vincent</a> was turned into a mosque.
</p><p>The Castilian nobleman Rodrigo Diaz de Vivar, known as <i><a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">El Cid</a></i>, in command of a combined Christian and Moorish army, besieged the city beginning in 1092. After the siege ended in May 1094, he ruled the city and its surrounding territory as his own fiefdom for five years from 15 June 1094 to July 1099.
</p><p>The city remained in the hands of Christian troops until 1102, when the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravids</a> retook the city and restored the Muslim religion. <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_VI_of_Le%C3%B3n_and_Castile" title="Alfonso VI of Le√≥n and Castile">Alfonso VI of Le√≥n and Castile</a>, drove them from the city, but was unable to hold it. The Almoravid <a href="/wiki/Mazdali_ibn_Tilankan" title="Mazdali ibn Tilankan">Mazdali</a> took possession on 5 May 1109, then the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohads</a>, seized control of it in 1171.
</p><p>Many Jews lived in Valencia during early Muslim rule, including the accomplished Jewish poet <a href="/wiki/Solomon_ibn_Gabirol" title="Solomon ibn Gabirol">Solomon ibn Gabirol</a>, who spent his last years in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Jews continued to live in Valencia throughout the Almoravid and Almohad dynasties, many of them being artisans such as silversmiths, shoemakers, blacksmiths, locksmiths, etc.; a few were rabbinic scholars. When the city fell to <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a>, the Jewish population of the city constituted about 7 percent of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christian_reconquest">Christian reconquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Christian reconquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerta_de_los_Serranos,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_86.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG/220px-Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG/330px-Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG/440px-Puerta_de_los_Serranos%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-30%2C_DD_86.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3942" data-file-height="2714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puerta_de_los_Serranos,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-30,_DD_86.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Torres_de_Serranos" title="Torres de Serranos">Towers of Serranos</a> is one of the twelve gates that guarded the Christian city walls of Valencia. Built between 1392 and 1398 in the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Gothic" title="Valencian Gothic">Valencian Gothic</a> style, this gate was used by kings to enter the city.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1238,<sup id="cite_ref-Guichard2001_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guichard2001-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a>, with an army composed of <a href="/wiki/Aragonese_people" title="Aragonese people">Aragonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalan people">Catalans</a>, Navarrese and crusaders from the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Calatrava" title="Order of Calatrava">Order of Calatrava</a>, laid siege to Valencia and on 28 September obtained a surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm1911-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Fifty thousand Moors were forced to leave.
</p><p>The city endured serious troubles in the mid-14th century, including the decimation of the population by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death of 1348</a> and subsequent years of epidemics ‚Äî as well as a series of wars and riots that followed. In 1391, the Jewish quarter was destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-Angel_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Angel-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 15th century was a time of economic expansion, known as the Valencian Golden Age, during which culture and the arts flourished. Concurrent population growth made Valencia the most populous city in the Crown of Aragon.
</p><p>Some of the most emblematic buildings of the city were built during this period, including the Serrans Towers (1392), the Silk Exchange (1482), the Micalet, and the Chapel of the Kings of the Convent of Sant Dom√®nec. In painting and sculpture, Flemish and Italian trends had an influence on Valencian artists.
</p><p>Valencia rose to become one of the most influential cities on the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a> in the 15th and 16th centuries. However, following the European discovery of the Americas, the Valencians, just like the Catalans, Aragonese and Majorcans, were unable to profit from participation in New World commerce due to their location far from the Atlantic coast. With this loss of trade, Valencia eventually suffered an economic crisis.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_century">17th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 17th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg/300px-Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="195" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg/450px-Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg/600px-Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="780" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Embarco_moriscos_en_el_Grao_de_valencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Expulsion of the Moriscos from Valencia Grau by Pere Oromig. Painting of 1616.</div></div></div>
<p>The crisis deepened during the 17th century with the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Moriscos" title="Expulsion of the Moriscos">expulsion</a> in 1609 of the Jews and the <a href="/wiki/Moriscos" class="mw-redirect" title="Moriscos">Moriscos</a>, descendants of the Muslim population that had converted to Christianity. The Spanish government systematically forced Moriscos to leave the kingdom for Muslim North Africa. They were concentrated in the former <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Aragon" title="Kingdom of Aragon">Kingdom of Aragon</a>, and in the Valencia area specifically, they constituted roughly a third of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The expulsion caused the financial ruin of some of the nobility and the bankruptcy of the Taula de Canvi financial institution in 1613.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The decline of the city reached its nadir with the <a href="/wiki/War_of_Spanish_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="War of Spanish Succession">War of Spanish Succession</a> (1702‚Äì1709), marking the end of the political and legal independence of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">Kingdom of Valencia</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, Valencia sided with the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> ruler of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles of Austria</a>. On 24 January 1706, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Mordaunt,_3rd_Earl_of_Peterborough" title="Charles Mordaunt, 3rd Earl of Peterborough">Charles Mordaunt, 3rd Earl of Peterborough, 1st Earl of Monmouth</a>, led a handful of English cavalrymen into the city after riding south from Barcelona, captured the nearby fortress at Sagunt, and bluffed the Spanish Bourbon army into withdrawal.
</p><p>The English held the city for 16 months and defeated several attempts to expel them. After the victory of the Bourbons at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Almansa" title="Battle of Almansa">Battle of Almansa</a> on 25 April 1707, the English army evacuated Valencia and <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a> ordered the repeal of the privileges of Valencia as punishment for the kingdom's support of Charles of Austria.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> By the Nueva Planta decrees <i>(Decretos de Nueva Planta)</i> the ancient <a href="/wiki/Furs_of_Valencia" title="Furs of Valencia">Charters of Valencia</a> were abolished and the city was governed by the Castilian Charter.
</p><p>The Valencian economy recovered during the 18th century with the rising manufacture of woven silk and ceramic tiles. The Palau de Just√≠cia is an example of the affluence manifested in the most prosperous times of Bourbon rule (1758‚Äì1802) during the rule of Charles III. The 18th century was the age of the Enlightenment in Europe, and its humanistic ideals influenced such men as Gregory Maians and Perez Bayer in Valencia, who maintained correspondence with the leading French and German thinkers of the time.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia,_1815,_Miquel_Parra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg/300px-Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg/450px-Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg/600px-Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_1815%2C_Miquel_Parra.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3691" data-file-height="2285" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrada_triomfal_de_Ferran_VII_a_Val%C3%A8ncia,_1815,_Miquel_Parra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Triumphal welcome of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a> at Valencia, 1814 by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Miguel_Parra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jos√© Miguel Parra (page does not exist)">Miquel Parra</a></div></div></div>
<p>The 19th century began with Spain embroiled in wars with France, Portugal, and England‚Äîbut the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">War of Independence</a> most affected the Valencian territories and the capital city. The repercussions of the French Revolution were still felt when Napoleon's armies invaded the Iberian Peninsula. The Valencian people rose up in arms against them on 23 May 1808, inspired by leaders such as Vicent Dom√©nech el Palleter.
</p><p>The mutineers seized the Citadel, a Supreme Junta government took over, and on 26‚Äì28 June, Napoleon's <a href="/wiki/Bon-Adrien_Jeannot_de_Moncey" title="Bon-Adrien Jeannot de Moncey">Marshal Moncey</a> attacked the city with a column of 9,000 French <a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Arm√©e">imperial</a> troops in the First Battle of Valencia. He failed to take the city in two assaults and retreated to Madrid. <a href="/wiki/Louis_Gabriel_Suchet" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis Gabriel Suchet">Marshal Suchet</a> began a long siege of the city in October 1811, and after intense bombardment forced it to surrender on 8 January 1812. After the capitulation, the French instituted reforms in Valencia, which became the capital of Spain when the <a href="/wiki/Bonapartism" title="Bonapartism">Bonapartist</a> pretender to the throne, Jos√© I (<a href="/wiki/Joseph_Bonaparte" title="Joseph Bonaparte">Joseph Bonaparte</a>, Napoleon's elder brother), moved the Court there in the middle of 1812. The disaster of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vitoria" title="Battle of Vitoria">Battle of Vitoria</a> on 21 June 1813 obliged Suchet to quit Valencia, and the French troops withdrew in July.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII</a> became king after the victorious end of the Peninsular War, which freed Spain from Napoleonic domination. When he returned on 24 March 1814 from exile in France, the Cortes requested that he respect the liberal Constitution of 1812, which seriously limited royal powers. Ferdinand refused and went to Valencia instead of Madrid. Here, on 17 April, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Javier_de_El%C3%ADo" title="Francisco Javier de El√≠o">General Elio</a> invited the King to reclaim his absolute rights and put his troops at the King's disposition. The king abolished the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1812" title="Spanish Constitution of 1812">Constitution of 1812</a> and dissolved the two chambers of the Spanish Parliament on 10 May. Thus began six years (1814‚Äì1820) of absolutist rule, but the constitution was reinstated during the <a href="/wiki/Trienio_Liberal" title="Trienio Liberal">Trienio Liberal</a>, a period of three years of liberal government in Spain from 1820‚Äì1823.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832,_per_A._Guesdon.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg/280px-Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg/420px-Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg/560px-Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832%2C_per_A._Guesdon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2515" data-file-height="1651" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Val%C3%A8ncia_el_1832,_per_A._Guesdon.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Valencia in 1832 by French <a href="/wiki/Guesdon" title="Guesdon">Alfred Guesdon</a></div></div></div>
<p>On the death of King Ferdinand VII in 1833, <a href="/wiki/Baldomero_Espartero,_Prince_of_Vergara" class="mw-redirect" title="Baldomero Espartero, Prince of Vergara">Baldomero Espartero</a> became one of the most ardent defenders of the hereditary rights of the king's daughter, the future <a href="/wiki/Isabel_II_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Isabel II of Spain">Isabella II</a>. During the regency of <a href="/wiki/Maria_Christina_of_the_Two_Sicilies" title="Maria Christina of the Two Sicilies">Maria Cristina</a>, Espartero ruled Spain for two years as its 18th Prime Minister from 16 September 1840 to 21 May 1841. City life in Valencia carried on in a revolutionary climate, with frequent clashes between liberals and republicans.
</p><p>The reign of Isabella II as an adult (1843‚Äì1868) was a period of relative stability and growth for Valencia. During the second half of the 19th century the bourgeoisie encouraged the development of the city and its environs; land-owners were enriched by the introduction of the orange crop and the expansion of vineyards and other crops,. This economic boom corresponded with a revival of local traditions and of the <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">Valencian</a> language, which had been ruthlessly suppressed from the time of Philip V. Around 1870, the Valencian Renaissance, a movement committed to the revival of the Valencian language and traditions, began to gain ascendancy.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century">20th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 20th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palaciow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Palaciow.jpg/220px-Palaciow.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Palaciow.jpg/330px-Palaciow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Palaciow.jpg/440px-Palaciow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palaciow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Palau de l'Exposici√≥</i> <i>(Palacio de la Exposici√≥n)</i>, site of Regional Exhibition of 1909</div></div></div>
<p>In the early 20th century Valencia was an industrialised city. The silk industry had disappeared, but there was a large production of hides and skins, wood, metals and foodstuffs, this last with substantial exports, particularly of wine and citrus. Small businesses predominated, but with the rapid mechanisation of industry larger companies were being formed. The best expression of this dynamic was in the regional exhibitions, including that of 1909 held next to the pedestrian avenue <i>L'Albereda</i> (<i>Paseo de la Alameda</i>), which depicted the progress of agriculture and industry. Among the most architecturally successful buildings of the era were those designed in the Art Nouveau style, such as the North Station <i>(Estaci√≥ del Nord)</i> and the Central and Columbus markets.
</p><p>World War I (1914‚Äì1918) greatly affected the Valencian economy, causing the collapse of its citrus exports.  The Second Spanish Republic (1931‚Äì1939) opened the way for democratic participation and the increased politicisation of citizens, especially in response to the rise of Conservative Front power in 1933. The inevitable march to civil war and the combat in Madrid resulted in the removal of the capital of the Republic to Valencia.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg/220px-Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg/330px-Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg/440px-Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="677" data-file-height="352" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Goverment_of_the_Spanish_Republic_in_Valencia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>After the continuous unsuccessful Francoist sieges on Madrid during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, the government of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">Republic of Spain</a> decreed Valencia as the capital of the country, from 7 November 1936 until 31 October 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>On 6 November 1936, the city became the capital of Republican Spain. The city was heavily bombarded by air and sea, and by the end of the war the city had survived 442 bombardments, leaving 2,831 dead and 847 wounded, although it is estimated that the death toll was higher. The Republican government moved to Barcelona on 31 October of that year. On 30 March 1939, Valencia surrendered and the Nationalist troops entered the city. The postwar years were a time of hardship for Valencians. During Franco's regime speaking or teaching <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">Valencian</a> was prohibited; in a significant reversal it is now compulsory for every schoolchild in Valencia.
</p><p>The dictatorship of Franco forbade political parties and began a harsh ideological and cultural repression countenanced<sup id="cite_ref-Reichardt2010_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Reichardt2010-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and sometimes led by the Catholic Church.<sup id="cite_ref-Tobin2007_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tobin2007-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BernanosCastillo2008_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BernanosCastillo2008-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The economy began to recover in the early 1960s, and the city experienced explosive population growth through immigration spurred by the jobs created with the implementation of major urban projects and infrastructure improvements. With the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">advent of democracy</a> in Spain, the ancient kingdom of Valencia was established as a new autonomous entity, the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian Community</a>, the Statute of Autonomy of 1982 designating Valencia as its capital.
</p><p>Valencia has since then experienced a surge in its cultural development, exemplified by exhibitions and performances at such iconic institutions as the <i>Palau de la M√∫sica</i>, the <i>Palacio de Congresos</i>, the Metro, the City of Arts and Sciences <i>(Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies)</i>, the Valencian Museum of Enlightenment and Modernity <i>(Museo Valenciano de la Ilustracion y la Modernidad)</i>, and the Institute of Modern Art <i>(Institut Valenci√† d'Art Modern)</i>. The various productions of <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, a renowned structural engineer, architect, and sculptor and of the architect <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Candela" title="F√©lix Candela">F√©lix Candela</a> have contributed to Valencia's international reputation. These public works and the ongoing rehabilitation of the Old City <i>(Ciutat Vella)</i> have helped improve the city's livability and tourism is continually increasing.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 9 July 2006, the World Day of Families, during Mass at Valencia's Cathedral, <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary" class="mw-redirect" title="Blessed Virgin Mary">Our Lady</a> of the Forsaken Basilica, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Benedict XVI">Pope Benedict XVI</a> used, the <i>Sant Calze</i>, a 1st-century Middle-Eastern artifact that some Catholics believe is the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Grail" title="Holy Grail">Holy Grail</a>. It was supposedly brought to that church by <a href="/wiki/Valerian_(emperor)" title="Valerian (emperor)">Emperor Valerian</a> in the 3rd century, after having been brought by <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">St. Peter</a> to Rome from Jerusalem. The <i>Sant Calze</i> (Holy Chalice) is a simple, small stone cup. Its base was added during the medieval period and consists of fine gold, alabaster and gem stones.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Valencia was selected in 2003 to host the historic <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Cup" title="America&#39;s Cup">America's Cup</a> yacht race, the first European city ever to do so. The <a href="/wiki/2007_America%27s_Cup" title="2007 America&#39;s Cup">America's Cup matches</a> took place from April to July 2007. On 3 July 2007, <a href="/wiki/Alinghi" title="Alinghi">Alinghi</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Team_New_Zealand" title="Team New Zealand">Team New Zealand</a> to retain the America's Cup. Twenty-two days later, on 25 July 2007, the leaders of the Alinghi syndicate, holder of the America's Cup, officially announced that Valencia would be the host city for the 33rd America's Cup, held in June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Valencia_City_Council_elections" title="Valencia City Council elections">Valencia City Council elections</a> from 1991 to 2015 the City Council was governed by the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People&#39;s Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> of Spain <i>(Partido Popular)</i> (PP) and Mayor <a href="/wiki/Rita_Barber%C3%A1_Nolla" class="mw-redirect" title="Rita Barber√° Nolla">Rita Barber√° Nolla</a> who became mayor by a pact made with the Valencian Union.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg/130px-SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg" decoding="async" width="130" height="368" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg/195px-SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg/260px-SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2832" data-file-height="8024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:SantaCatalina_-_Vertorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Baroque belfry of the Gothic <a href="/wiki/Santa_Catalina,_Valencia" title="Santa Catalina, Valencia">Santa Catalina church</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Major monuments include <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Cathedral" title="Valencia Cathedral">Valencia Cathedral</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Torres_de_Serranos" title="Torres de Serranos">Torres de Serrans</a></i>, the <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Torres_de_Quart&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Torres de Quart (page does not exist)">Torres de Quart</a></i> (<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torres_de_Quart" class="extiw" title="es:Torres de Quart">es:Torres de Quart</a>), the <i><a href="/wiki/Llotja_de_la_Seda" title="Llotja de la Seda">Llotja de la Seda</a></i> (declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1996), and the <i><a href="/wiki/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies">Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies</a></i> (City of Arts and Sciences), an entertainment-based cultural and architectural complex designed by <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a> and <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Candela" title="F√©lix Candela">F√©lix Candela</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CAC_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAC-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Museu_de_Belles_Arts_de_Val%C3%A8ncia" title="Museu de Belles Arts de Val√®ncia">Museu de Belles Arts de Val√®ncia</a></i> houses a large collection of paintings from the 14th to the 18th centuries, including works by <a href="/wiki/Vel%C3%A1zquez" class="mw-redirect" title="Vel√°zquez">Vel√°zquez</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Goya" class="mw-redirect" title="Goya">Goya</a>, as well as an important series of engravings by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Battista_Piranesi" title="Giovanni Battista Piranesi">Piranesi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Institut_Valenci%C3%A0_d%27Art_Modern" title="Institut Valenci√† d&#39;Art Modern">Institut Valenci√† d'Art Modern</a></i> (Valencian Institute of Modern Art) houses both permanent collections and temporary exhibitions of contemporary art and photography.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The ancient winding streets of the Barrio del Carmen contain buildings dating to <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Arabic</a> times. The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mary_of_Valencia_Cathedral" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Mary of Valencia Cathedral">Cathedral</a>, built between the 13th and 15th centuries, is primarily of <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Gothic" title="Valencian Gothic">Valencian Gothic</a> style but contains elements of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque architecture</a>. Beside the Cathedral is the Gothic <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">Basilica</a> of the Virgin <i>(Bas√≠lica De La Mare de D√©u dels Desamparats)</i>. The 15th-century <i>Serrans</i> and <i>Quart</i> towers are part of what was once the wall surrounding the city.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> has recognised the Silk Exchange market <i>(<a href="/wiki/Llotja_de_la_Seda" title="Llotja de la Seda">La Llotja de la Seda</a>)</i>, erected in early Valencian Gothic style, as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Central Market (<i><a href="/wiki/Mercado_Central,_Valencia" title="Mercado Central, Valencia">Mercat Central</a></i>) in <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Art_Nouveau" title="Valencian Art Nouveau">Valencian Art Nouveau</a> style, is one of the largest in Europe. The main railway station <i>Estaci√≥ Del Nord</i> is built in <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Art_Nouveau" title="Valencian Art Nouveau">Valencian Art Nouveau</a> (a Spanish version of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>) style.
</p><p>World-renowned (and city-born) architect <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a> produced the futuristic City of Arts and Sciences <i>(<a href="/wiki/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies">Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies</a>)</i>, which contains an opera house/performing <a href="/wiki/Arts_centre" title="Arts centre">arts centre</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Science_museum" title="Science museum">science museum</a>, an <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cinema/planetarium, an oceanographic park and other structures such as a long covered walkway and restaurants. Calatrava is also responsible for the bridge named after him in the centre of the city. The Music Palace <i>(<a href="/w/index.php?title=Palau_De_La_M%C3%BAsica&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Palau De La M√∫sica (page does not exist)">Palau De La M√∫sica</a>) (<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palacio_de_la_M%C3%BAsica_de_Valencia" class="extiw" title="es:Palacio de la M√∫sica de Valencia">es:Palacio de la M√∫sica de Valencia</a>)</i> is another noteworthy example of modern architecture in Valencia.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_cathedral">The cathedral</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: The cathedral">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg/220px-Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="290" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg/330px-Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg/440px-Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2046" data-file-height="2694" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cimbori_almoina_abril_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northern view of the cathedral: dome, apse, and the Basilica of Our Lady</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Cathedral" title="Valencia Cathedral">Valencia Cathedral</a> was called <i>Iglesia Major</i> in the early days of the <i>Reconquista</i>, then <i>Iglesia de la Seu</i> (<i>Seu</i> is from the Latin <i>sedes</i>, i.e., (archiepiscopal) See), and by virtue of the papal concession of 16 October 1866, it was called the <i>Basilica Metropolitana</i>. It is situated in the centre of the ancient Roman city where some believe the temple of Diana stood. In Gothic times, it seems to have been dedicated to the Holy Saviour; <a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">the Cid</a> dedicated it to the Blessed Virgin; King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a> did likewise, leaving in the main chapel the image of the Blessed Virgin, which he carried with him and is reputed to be the one now preserved in the sacristy. The Moorish mosque, which had been converted into a <a href="/wiki/Christian_Church" title="Christian Church">Christian Church</a> by the conqueror, was deemed unworthy of the title of the cathedral of Valencia, and in 1262 Bishop Andr√©s de Albalat laid the cornerstone of the new Gothic building, with three naves; these reach only to the choir of the present building. Bishop Vidal de Blanes built the chapter hall, and James I added the tower, called <i>El Micalet</i> because it was blessed on St. Michael's day in 1418. The tower is about 58 metres (190 feet) high and is topped with a <a href="/wiki/Bell_tower" title="Bell tower">belfry</a> (1660‚Äì1736).
</p><p>In the 15th century the dome was added and the naves extended back of the choir, uniting the building to the tower and forming a main entrance. Archbishop Luis Alfonso de los Cameros began the building of the main chapel in 1674; the walls were decorated with marbles and bronzes in the <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> style of that period. At the beginning of the 18th century the German Conrad Rudolphus built the fa√ßade of the main entrance. The other two doors lead into the transept; one, that of the Apostles in pure pointed Gothic, dates from the 14th century, the other is that of the Palau. The additions made to the back of the cathedral detract from its height. The 18th-century restoration rounded the pointed arches, covered the Gothic columns with <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_order" title="Corinthian order">Corinthian</a> pillars, and redecorated the walls.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia_Water_Court.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Valencia_Water_Court.JPG/220px-Valencia_Water_Court.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Valencia_Water_Court.JPG/330px-Valencia_Water_Court.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Valencia_Water_Court.JPG/440px-Valencia_Water_Court.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2297" data-file-height="1759" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia_Water_Court.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sitting of the <a href="/wiki/Water_Tribunal_of_the_plain_of_Valencia" title="Water Tribunal of the plain of Valencia"><i>Tribunal de les Aig√ºes</i></a> outside the Portal of the Apostles of the Valencia Cathedral</div></div></div>
<p>The dome has no lantern, its plain ceiling being pierced by two large side windows. There are four chapels on either side, besides that at the end and those that open into the choir, the transept, and the sanctuary. It contains many paintings by eminent artists. A silver <a href="/wiki/Reredos" title="Reredos">reredos</a>, which was behind the altar, was carried away in the war of 1808, and converted into coin to meet the expenses of the campaign. There are two paintings by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Goya" title="Francisco Goya">Francisco de Goya</a> in the San Francesco chapel. Behind the Chapel of the <a href="/wiki/Blessed_Sacrament" title="Blessed Sacrament">Blessed Sacrament</a> is a small <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> chapel built by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Calixtus_III" class="mw-redirect" title="Pope Calixtus III">Calixtus III</a>. Beside the cathedral is the chapel dedicated to the Our Lady of the Forsaken <i>(<a href="/wiki/Virgen_de_los_desamparados" title="Virgen de los desamparados">Mare de D√©u dels desamparats</a>)</i>.
</p><p>The <i>Tribunal de les Aig√ºes</i> (Water Court), a court dating from Moorish times that hears and mediates in matters relating to irrigation water, sits at noon every Thursday outside the <i>Porta dels Apostols</i> (Portal of the Apostles).<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hospital">Hospital</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hospital">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palau_generalitat9.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Palau_generalitat9.jpg/220px-Palau_generalitat9.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Palau_generalitat9.jpg/330px-Palau_generalitat9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Palau_generalitat9.jpg/440px-Palau_generalitat9.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2208" data-file-height="2056" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palau_generalitat9.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Palau de la <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_Valenciana" title="Generalitat Valenciana">Generalitat Valenciana</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1409, a hospital was founded and placed under the <a href="/wiki/Patronage" title="Patronage">patronage</a> of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_de_los_Inocentes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Santa Mar√≠a de los Inocentes (page does not exist)">Santa Maria dels Innocents</a>; to this was attached a confraternity devoted to recovering the bodies of the unfriended dead in the city and within a radius of 5&#160;km around it. At the end of the 15th century this confraternity separated from the hospital, and continued its work under the name of "Cofradia para el √°mparo de los desamparados". King <a href="/wiki/Philip_IV_of_Spain" title="Philip IV of Spain">Philip IV of Spain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Arcos" title="Duke of Arcos">Duke of Arcos</a> suggested the building of the new chapel, and in 1647 the <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">Viceroy</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Conde_de_Oropesa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Conde de Oropesa (page does not exist)">Conde de Oropesa</a>, who had been preserved from <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">the bubonic plague</a>, insisted on carrying out their project. The Blessed Virgin was proclaimed patroness of the city under the title of <i>Virgen de los desamparados</i> (Virgin of the Forsaken), and Archbishop Pedro de Urbina, on 31 June 1652, laid the cornerstone of the new chapel of this name. The archiepiscopal palace, a grain market in the time of the Moors, is simple in design, with an inside cloister and achapel. In 1357, the arch that connects it with the cathedral was built. Inside the council chamber are preserved the portraits of all the prelates of Valencia.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_churches">Medieval churches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Medieval churches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_los_Juanes,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-29,_DD_19.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG/220px-Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="215" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG/330px-Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG/440px-Iglesia_de_los_Juanes%2C_Valencia%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2014-06-29%2C_DD_19.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3311" data-file-height="3234" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iglesia_de_los_Juanes,_Valencia,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2014-06-29,_DD_19.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sant Joan del Mercat church (14th c.-1700)</div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Santos_Juanes,_Valencia" title="Santos Juanes, Valencia">Sant Joan del Mercat</a>- Gothic parish church dedicated to John the Baptist and Evangelist, rebuilt in Baroque style after a 1598 fire. The interior ceilings was frescoed by <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Palomino" title="Antonio Palomino">Palomino</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_San_Nicol%C3%A1s_(Valencia)" title="Church of San Nicol√°s (Valencia)">Sant Nicolau</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Santa_Catalina,_Valencia" title="Santa Catalina, Valencia">Santa Catalina</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iglesia_de_San_Esteban,_Valencia" class="mw-redirect" title="Iglesia de San Esteban, Valencia">Sant Esteve</a></li></ul>
<p><i>El Temple</i> (the Temple), the ancient church of the <a href="/wiki/Knights_Templar" title="Knights Templar">Knights Templar</a>, which passed into the hands of the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Montesa" title="Order of Montesa">Order of Montesa</a> and was rebuilt in the reigns of <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VI_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VI of Spain">Ferdinand VI</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III</a>; the former convent of the <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Order" title="Dominican Order">Dominicans</a>, at one time the headquarters of the <i>Capitan General</i>, the cloister of which has a Gothic wing and chapter room, large columns imitating <a href="/wiki/Arecaceae" title="Arecaceae">palm trees</a>; the <i>Colegio del Corpus Christi</i>, which is devoted to the Blessed Sacrament, and in which <a href="/wiki/Eucharistic_adoration" title="Eucharistic adoration">perpetual adoration</a> is carried on; the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> college, which was destroyed in 1868 by the revolutionary Committee of the Popular Front, but later rebuilt; and the <i>Colegio de San Juan</i> (also of the Society), the former college of the nobles, now a provincial institute for secondary instruction.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Squares_and_gardens">Squares and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Squares and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia,_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG/220px-Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG/330px-Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG/440px-Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia%2C_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3664" data-file-height="2748" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pla%C3%A7a_de_l%27Ajuntament_de_Val%C3%A8ncia,_Pa%C3%ADs_Valenci%C3%A0.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pla√ßa de l'Ajuntament</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_city_squares_by_size" title="List of city squares by size">largest plaza</a> in Valencia is the <i>Pla√ßa del Ajuntament</i>; it is home to the City Hall <i>(Ajuntament)</i> on its western side and the central post office <i>(Edifici de Correus)</i> on its eastern side, a cinema that shows classic movies, and many restaurants and bars. The plaza is triangular in shape, with a large cement lot at the southern end, normally surrounded by flower vendors. It serves as ground zero during the <a href="/wiki/Falles" title="Falles">Les Falles</a> when the fireworks of the <i><a href="/wiki/Masclet%C3%A0" title="Masclet√†">Masclet√†</a></i> can be heard every afternoon. There is a large fountain at the northern end.
</p><p>The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Mare_de_D%C3%A9u&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pla√ßa de la Mare de D√©u (page does not exist)">Pla√ßa de la Mare de D√©u</a></i> contains the Basilica of the Virgin and the Turia fountain, and is a popular spot for locals and tourists. Around the corner is the Pla√ßa de la Reina, with the Cathedral, orange trees, and many bars and restaurants.
</p><p>
The <a href="/wiki/Turia_(river)" title="Turia (river)">Turia River</a> was diverted in the 1960s, after <a href="/wiki/1957_Valencia_flood" title="1957 Valencia flood">severe flooding</a>, and the old riverbed is now the Turia gardens, which contain a children's playground, a fountain, and sports fields.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg/220px-Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg/330px-Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg/440px-Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="963" data-file-height="589" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Antiguo-cauce-del-r%C3%ADo-Turia-3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Garden in Turia River</div></div></div><p>  The <i>Palau de la M√∫sica</i> is adjacent to the Turia gardens and the City of Arts and Sciences lies at one end. The <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Bioparc" title="Valencia Bioparc">Valencia Bioparc</a> is a zoo, also located in the Turia riverbed.
</p><p>Other gardens in Valencia include:
</p>
<ul><li>The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jardines_de_Monforte&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jardines de Monforte (page does not exist)">Jard√≠ns de Monfort</a></i> (<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jardines_de_Monforte" class="extiw" title="es:Jardines de Monforte">es:Jardines de Monforte</a>).</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jardin_Botanico_(Valencia)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jardin Botanico (Valencia) (page does not exist)">Jard√≠ Bot√†nic</a></i> (Botanical Gardens).</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jardines_del_Real&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jardines del Real (page does not exist)">Jard√≠ns del Real</a></i> or <i>Jard√≠ns de Vivers</i> (Del Real Gardens), they are located in the Pla del Real district, on just the former site of the <a href="/wiki/Real_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Real Palace">Del Real Palace</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg/200px-Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg/300px-Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg/400px-Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2776" data-file-height="1851" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies">Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies</a> complex designed by the architects the Valencian <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a> and Madrilenian <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Candela" title="F√©lix Candela">F√©lix Candela</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg/200px-Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg/300px-Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg/400px-Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1492" data-file-height="739" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Valencia-L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic" title="L&#39;Oceanogr√†fic">L'Oceanogr√†fic</a>, located within the complex of the Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies, is currently the largest aquarium in Europe, it houses 45,000 animals of 500 species.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ciutat_de_les_Arts_i_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies">Ciutat de les Arts i les Ci√®ncies</a> (City of Arts and Sciences<i>). Designed by the Valencian architect <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, it is situated in the former T√∫ria river-bed and comprises the following monuments:</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Palau_de_les_Arts_Reina_Sof%C3%ADa" class="mw-redirect" title="Palau de les Arts Reina Sof√≠a">Palau de les Arts Reina Sof√≠a</a>, a flamboyant opera and music palace with four halls and a total area of 37,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (398,000&#160;sq&#160;ft).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/L%27Oceanogr%C3%A0fic" title="L&#39;Oceanogr√†fic">L'Oceanogr√†fic</a>, the largest aquarium in Europe, with a variety of ocean beings from different environments: from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean</a>, fishes from the ocean and reef inhabitants, <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">sharks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">mackerel</a> swarms, <a href="/wiki/Dolphinarium" title="Dolphinarium">dolphinarium</a>, inhabitants of the <a href="/wiki/Polar_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Polar region">polar regions</a> (<a href="/wiki/Beluga_(whale)" class="mw-redirect" title="Beluga (whale)">belugas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walrus" title="Walrus">walruses</a>, penguins), coast inhabitants (sea lions), etc. L'Oceanogr√†fic exhibits also smaller animals as <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jellyfish" title="Jellyfish">jellyfish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_anemone" title="Sea anemone">sea anemones</a>, etc.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/El_Museu_de_les_Ci%C3%A8ncies_Pr%C3%ADncipe_Felipe" class="mw-redirect" title="El Museu de les Ci√®ncies Pr√≠ncipe Felipe">El Museu de les Ci√®ncies Pr√≠ncipe Felipe</a>, an interactive museum of science but resembling the skeleton of a whale. It has an area of around 40,000 square metres (430,556 square feet) over three floors.</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=L%27Hemisf%C3%A8ric&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="L&#39;Hemisf√®ric (page does not exist)">L'Hemisf√®ric</a>, an Imax cinema. (<a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/L%27Hemisf%C3%A8ric" class="extiw" title="es:L&#39;Hemisf√®ric">es:L'Hemisf√®ric</a>)</li></ul></li>
<li>Museu de Prehist√≤ria de Val√®ncia (Prehistory Museum of Valencia)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Valencian_Museum_of_Ethnology" title="Valencian Museum of Ethnology">Museu Valenci√† d'Etnologia</a> (Valencian Museum of Ethnology)</li>
<li>House Museum <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Blasco_Ib%C3%A1%C3%B1ez" title="Vicente Blasco Ib√°√±ez">Blasco Ib√°√±ez</a></li>
<li>IVAM ‚Äì Institut Valenci√† d'Art Modern ‚Äì Centre Julio Gonz√°lez <i>Julio Gonz√°lez Centre ‚Äì Valencian Institute of Modern Art</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Museu_de_Belles_Arts_San_P%C3%ADo_V" class="mw-redirect" title="Museu de Belles Arts San P√≠o V">Museu de Belles Arts de Val√®ncia</a> (Museum of Fine Arts)</li>
